  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_16b3daa0-d1f6-4363-904d-6da6c96d2be3'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

<span id="freeTextContainer16215410730747802854"><b>
  <b>The sequel to the instant </b>

    <i>New York Times</i>

  <span id="freeText16215410730747802854" style="display:none"><b>
  <b>The sequel to the instant </b>
  <b>
    <i>New York Times</i>
  </b>
  <b> bestseller that was "made for fans of Victoria Aveyard and Sabaa Tahir" (</b>
  <b>
    <i>Bustle</i>
  </b>
  <b>), </b>
  <b>
    <i>Lady Smoke</i>
  </b>
  <b> is an epic new fantasy about a throne cruelly stolen and a girl who must fight to take it back for her people.</b>
</b><br /><br />The Kaiser murdered Theodosia's mother, the Fire Queen, when Theo was only six. He took Theo's country and kept her prisoner, crowning her Ash Princess--a pet to toy with and humiliate for ten long years. That era has ended. The Kaiser thought his prisoner weak and defenseless. He didn't realize that a sharp mind is the deadliest weapon.<br /><br />Theo no longer wears a crown of ashes. She has taken back her rightful title, and a hostage--Prinz Soren. But her people remain enslaved under the Kaiser's rule, and now she is thousands of miles away from them and her throne.<br /><br />To get them back, she will need an army. Only, securing an army means she must trust her aunt, the dreaded pirate Dragonsbane. And according to Dragonsbane, an army can only be produced if Theo takes a husband. Something an Astrean Queen has never done.<br /><br />Theo knows that freedom comes at a price, but she is determined to find a way to save her country without losing herself.<br /><br />"<b>A darkly enchanting page-turner</b> you won't be able to put down." -<i>-Bustle</i> on <i>Ash Princess, </i> Book 1 in the Ash Princess series</span>

<div id="review_2648502745" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2648502745" />
    <a title="Cesar" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34467577-cesar"><img alt="Cesar" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1501005350p2/34467577.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2648502745?book_show_action=true">Feb 19, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cesar" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cesar" href="/user/show/34467577-cesar">Cesar</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2648502745" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8686142945157427853">4 stars.<br/><br/><b>Lady Smoke</b> has exceeded my expectations. Usually, in a trilogy, there's always the chance where the second book suffers from Second Book Syndrome. To me, Lady Smoke was a pretty damn good installment to the Ash Princess trilogy.<br/><br/>Mind you, this will not be for everyone as I will explain further, but for a second book, I was really impressed by how the story progressed as well as the stakes that were involved.<br/><br/>Lady Smoke takes place right after the events of Ash Princess where Theodosia esca</span>
  <span id="freeText8686142945157427853" style="display:none">4 stars.<br /><br /><b>Lady Smoke</b> has exceeded my expectations. Usually, in a trilogy, there's always the chance where the second book suffers from Second Book Syndrome. To me, Lady Smoke was a pretty damn good installment to the Ash Princess trilogy.<br /><br />Mind you, this will not be for everyone as I will explain further, but for a second book, I was really impressed by how the story progressed as well as the stakes that were involved.<br /><br />Lady Smoke takes place right after the events of Ash Princess where Theodosia escapes her homeland and is trying to form an alliance with another country in hopes of taking back Astrea and defeat the Kaiser. The only problem is, she has to take on a husband, something a queen has never done in Astrea.<br /><br />Earlier, I mentioned that this won't be for everyone. While I did like Lady Smoke, I can see how this won't be everyone's cup of tea. I wouldn't call this a political story because while there is mention of arranged marriage and armies, the politics are not as prevalent. And there is a love triangle which I'll admit, did bother me somewhat. So keep that in mind when going into the story.<br /><br />Lady Smoke delves more into the idea of doing whatever it takes to do what is right even if it means giving up your pride and accepting help. Or, use that pride to make sense of the situation and still do the right thing. <br /><br />Theo is put on a pedestal where she has to make very important choices that will determine the fate of Astrea and its people. But having to choose a partner means forsaking what Theo believes in. And this is where I like her more as a character. She only became a queen and she still has a lot of learning and growing up to do. Others may respect her like a queen, but she has to work on acting like one. The novel does take on a feminist approach and I applaud Theo for standing up for not only her country but for herself. <br /><br />The story itself is unapologetically true in the aspect of refugees and how they are treated. This isn't a spoiler since in the first book there is mention of refugee camps in different countries. And when Theo visits a camp in a country she is temporarily staying in, she is taken aback by how the treatment of refugees. You want to look away but the reality of it is very shocking. Not to mention this is something that is still happening in our world. I'm glad this was brought up so it can give readers an insight into the subject.<br /><br />The reason this got a 4-star rating is because of one thing: The love triangle.<br /><br />I am not against love triangles or the idea of them. If done right, I can enjoy it. My main issue with this love triangle is that it feels unnecessary and forced. It was unnecessary because it didn't add anything to the story. It might have given us more insight into Blaise and Soren, but it felt redundant in the grand scheme of Theo trying to take back her country. Not to mention Blaise is a boring love interest. I'm all for Soren. <br /><br />The love triangle was also forced because it didn't need to be there. I get that Blaise and Theo were close to each other, but his feelings for her aren't as genuine. It's like he was only there just to be a love interest. He does have some growth here in Lady Smoke, but he didn't need to be a love interest.<br /><br />The whole friends-to-lover trope is a good one and can be done very well, but not every friend of the main character has to be a romance option.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Verdict</u>
</b><br /><br />Lady Smoke is a good follow up to Ash Princess. It's not perfect, but the story and Theo do make up for it by showing us what Theo has to do in harsh times as well as diving into how cruel the world can be. I'm really looking forward to the final book.<br /><br />Thanks for reading my review!<br /><br />-Cesar</span>
  <a data-text-id="8686142945157427853" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2449744164" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2449744164" />
    <a title="Helena of Eretz ✰" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27036454-helena-of-eretz"><img alt="Helena of Eretz ✰" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596076376p2/27036454.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2449744164?book_show_action=true">Aug 23, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Helena of Eretz ✰" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Helena of Eretz ✰" href="/user/show/27036454-helena-of-eretz">Helena of Eretz ✰</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=hardback">hardback</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2449744164" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7587082070366790048">This series is slowly, but surely, becoming a <b>new favourite</b> of mine. I expected this instalment to suffer from <i>Second Book Syndrome</i>, but I’m happy to announce that it didn’t! There was no lull in the action or fluff in the story. Rather, the plot kept me <b>riveted and stressed</b> over the safety of my favourite characters. <br/><br/><b>Theo</b> is such a wonderful protagonist and queen who truly wants to do right by her people. <b>Søren</b>, often a lad in distress, unfortunately, is such a sweet, but protective, character </span>
  <span id="freeText7587082070366790048" style="display:none">This series is slowly, but surely, becoming a <b>new favourite</b> of mine. I expected this instalment to suffer from <i>Second Book Syndrome</i>, but I’m happy to announce that it didn’t! There was no lull in the action or fluff in the story. Rather, the plot kept me <b>riveted and stressed</b> over the safety of my favourite characters. <br /><br /><b>Theo</b> is such a wonderful protagonist and queen who truly wants to do right by her people. <b>Søren</b>, often a lad in distress, unfortunately, is such a sweet, but protective, character that I absolutely adore. <b>Blaise</b>, the other side of the love triangle, is so loyal and devoted to Theo. <b>Art and Heron</b> are steadfast in their support of her, as well. I also loved <b>Erik and Hoa</b>. Theo truly has such a strong support system around her. <br /><br />Unsurprisingly, I can’t wait to see <b>Cress’</b> downfall. I didn’t like her from the beginning of <i>Ash Princess</i> and I can’t bloody stand her now. I can’t wait to see her and Theo finally go head to head in the finale. <br /><br />I really appreciated the discussion of the treatment of <b>refugees</b> in this book, though. It’s an important topic that’s not normally included, and for that reason alone, I think that it makes <i>Lady Smoke</i> an even stronger book. Oftentimes, in YA fantasy, we see a queen wanting to liberate her people, but very rarely do we get to see the <b>treatment</b> of the aforementioned people. I’m really pleased that Laura Sebastian chose to include this <b>controversial discussion</b> that affects many around the world today. <br /><br />My only complaint, really, is the inclusion of a <b>love triangle</b>. While it’s fairly obvious who Theo prefers, I don’t think it was completely necessary to propel the plot forward. I personally believe that book characters can be close without having to be in love with one another...or maybe that’s just me. <i>*shrugs*</i><br /><br />I found <i>Lady Smoke</i> to be a worthy instalment of this trilogy and <i>CANNOT WAIT</i> until the finale this coming spring. I’d definitely recommend this series to fans of the <i>Winner’s Curse</i> trilogy, who are impatiently waiting for the spinoff, the <i>Midnight Lie</i>...also releasing in the spring, haha.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7587082070366790048" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2733059193" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2733059193" />
    <a title="Dannii Elle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44487975-dannii-elle"><img alt="Dannii Elle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508499419p2/44487975.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2733059193?book_show_action=true">Mar 02, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dannii Elle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dannii Elle" href="/user/show/44487975-dannii-elle">Dannii Elle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/42743065-lady-smoke">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44487975-dannii-elle?shelf=fantastic-fabrications">fantastic-fabrications</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2733059193" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4951694057706272109"><b>First Read: March 2019, Rating 4.5 Stars<br/>Second Read: November 2020, Rating 4 Stars</b><br/><br/>This is the second instalment in The Ash Princess series.<br/><br/>Theodosia is the last remaining heir of a vanquished country, now owned by its conqueror and the man who kept her a beaten and paraded captive, for almost her entire childhood. But this once Ash Princess is now determined to fulfil her role as Queen Theo, and this queen wants her land back and her people freed.<br/><br/>The Theo the reader was introduced to in the prev</span>
  <span id="freeText4951694057706272109" style="display:none"><b>First Read: March 2019, Rating 4.5 Stars<br />Second Read: November 2020, Rating 4 Stars</b><br /><br />This is the second instalment in The Ash Princess series.<br /><br />Theodosia is the last remaining heir of a vanquished country, now owned by its conqueror and the man who kept her a beaten and paraded captive, for almost her entire childhood. But this once Ash Princess is now determined to fulfil her role as Queen Theo, and this queen wants her land back and her people freed.<br /><br />The Theo the reader was introduced to in the previous series instalment is a very different being to the one that appeared here. Theo's original wishes were almost solely those of self-preservation. This was understandable. But the continued harsh treatment and exposure to the pain of both herself and her people slowly whittled away this softer exterior to reveal an inner-core of strength that disallowed either to become the playthings of another, ever again. No matter the cost. Her resolve has hardened and, with it, my love for her character is complete.<br /><br />However, I often found adoration for Theo divided, as the other lovable characters, who made up her inner-circle, battled for their rightful place in my heart, too. This band of vicious, little rouges made this story as bad-ass and bloody as they did unbearably sweet, and I bonded with them as truly as they did with one another. Theo, on her own, was enough to make me a passionate advocate for this series but her loyal companions, dogging her journey every step of the way, made this a truly unputdownable and continually fraught yet fascinating read. It is a very rare book that can make me soar through 500 pages in a handful of hours, foregoing a good night's sleep in the process. I did this during both readings of the book.<br /><br />As these characters fled from the Kaiser who sought to imprison them, the geography of the land was further revealed to the reader. I loved learning more about this world and the unique politics that governed each realm. It seemed the Kaiser was not the only corrupt player and Theo and her crew must once again concern themselves with all the court niceties and underhand political scheming necessary to get their freedom returned to them.<br /><br />I have so far only waxed lyrical about all the aspects I love about this novel but the aspect I appreciated the absolute most were the feminist vibes that were evident throughout. Theo is not playing games in this book! She has no qualms about calling out the patriarchal system that advocates for the unequal alignment for the gender of its people. She also calls into question outdated traditions that further bias this inequality, and are accepted due to nothing more than the length of time their practise has been committed to memory.<br /><br />Sebastian steeped this entire book with the embodiment of female empowerment and I appreciate her so much for doing so. One other such instance is that virginity is not imbued with any social significance and, as such, the word does not even exist in most languages. By providing the reader with a fantastical parallel to such accepted real-world issues it calls into question, in the most thought-provoking of ways, the inequality that exists outside of these pages. This is one feminist novel not to be missed!<br /><br />I received a copy of this book in exchange for an honest review. Thank you to the author, Laura Sebastian, and the publisher, Macmillan, for this opportunity.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4951694057706272109" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2372791600" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer13032095655163902656">9/28/18<br/><b>...an army can only be produced if Theo takes a husband.</b><br/><p>
  <a href='https://giphy.com/gifs/rita-ora-457NTDOuMmDfO' rel='nofollow noopener'>via GIPHY</a>
</p><br/>But seriously, like wtf why!? <div id="review_3280208507" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3280208507" />
    <a title="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66224803-jessi-h-vojsk"><img alt="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597641717p2/66224803.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3280208507?book_show_action=true">Apr 19, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" href="/user/show/66224803-jessi-h-vojsk">Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3280208507" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10166319432671196873"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1462408788ra/18993807.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i> “Still, you reminded me of the legend. <br/>With your bright eyes and crown of ashes and Fire Queen mother. <br/>Lady Thora, everyone called you, but I thought of you as Lady Smoke. <br/>I knew it would only be a matter of time before your ember sparked again, until you once more burned bright enough to escape him.”</i><br/><br/>Story 🌟🌟🌟🌟<br/>Theo escaped the Kaiser and his court only to be forced into another country filled with intrigues. Princes, other countries are fighting for Theos hand, but every time she chooses a way </span>
  <span id="freeText10166319432671196873" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1462408788ra/18993807.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i> “Still, you reminded me of the legend. <br>With your bright eyes and crown of ashes and Fire Queen mother. <br>Lady Thora, everyone called you, but I thought of you as Lady Smoke. <br>I knew it would only be a matter of time before your ember sparked again, until you once more burned bright enough to escape him.”</i><br><br>Story 🌟🌟🌟🌟<br>Theo escaped the Kaiser and his court only to be forced into another country filled with intrigues. Princes, other countries are fighting for Theos hand, but every time she chooses a way the Kaiser destroys it. <br>But Theo didn’t suffer so long only to give up so easily. <br>War longs for sacrifice, but sacrifice doesn’t come easily for Theo, who never had much and who now wants to protect it under all cost. <br><br>Oh this one was as good as the first. It was filled with intrigues, action and even war. <br>And the plot twists were amazing! <br><br>Character 🌟🌟🌟🌟<br><br><i> “Friends, enemies, I don’t think it matters anymore. The chains are just as heavy, no matter who holds the key,” he says.</i><br><br>Even though Theo had a huge character development in the first book, she didn’t stop there. With every problem coming, she grew and it’s amazing. <br>And even though she is the queen, she’s not perfect. But she fights with every breath she takes. <br>And I love her for that. <br>In the first book I couldn’t choose between Blaise and Soren. But now I can. <br>I choose Soren. Enemies prince, warrior and suffering big hearted guy? That’s my type. <br>But again in my way he didn’t have enough pages in this book. <br>Same with Blaise. <br>But now I know why. Blaise and Soren were never intended to be main characters. <br>Theo is the only one. They’re just part of the story. <br>Like the other side characters, there are just here to drive the plot onward. <br>All in all the author again did a great job. <br>All the new side characters pushed the story in the right direction and the plot twists made it even better. <br><br>Relationships 🌟🌟🌟<br><br><i> “I don’t want to protect you. <br>I don’t need to protect you. <br>You have others for that and you’ve done it yourself enough times by now. <br>I don’t want to run away with you; <br>I want to stand at your side and fight—fight for something I never even thought that I wanted, but I do. <br>I’m stronger with you, and braver, and I never want to go back to living like I was before. <br>I love you, and it isn’t anything to do with who you pretended to be. <br>I love you.”</i><br><br>I had high hopes for the second book. High hopes of finally being able to choose. <br>And I did! Hallelujah! <br>Like I said: my vote goes to - Soren! Wooohooo. <br>But Theo isn’t like me. She can’t choose. She switches between those two throughout the story and it breaks my heart. Those poor boys love the same girl and they couldn’t be any more different. <br>A relationship I loved in this book was the one between the shadows and Theo. <br>They were a loyal front, worked together, planned together. They were a team. <br>And I loved that. <br><br>World 🌟🌟🌟🌟<br><br><i> “In Goraki, there is a legend of a bird made of fire,” she says. <br>“It never dies, the Phiren. <br>First, it is made of embers, glowing bright and new before they burst into flames. <br>The Phiren burns brightly for many years, but no fire burns forever—it is smothered into a bird of smoke, wispy and dark. <br>It stays like that for a stretch of time—sometimes centuries even—but the day always comes when an ember within it sparks and its life begins anew.”</i><br><br>Writing style 🌟🌟🌟🌟🌟<br>The writing improved and I loved it. <br>It was again in Theos POV filled with a lot of plot and a lot of emotions, thoughts, doubts. <br>There were quotes I loved and they definitely made it into my top favorite quotes. <br><br><i> “I died the Queen of Peace, and peace died with me,” she says after a moment. <br>“But you are the Queen of Flame and Fury, Theodosia, and you will set their world on fire.”</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="10166319432671196873" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17516372049906015147">It was good.. but god dammit - I hate love triangles. <br/><br/>Okay, I keep changing my mind on this freaking book rating. I can't decide to put a 3 or 4 star... so it'll be a freaking 3.5. Like I mentioned above, <i>Lady Smoke</i> was a good book. I have the audio version, which definitely makes it a bit easier for myself when working such long drastic hours. Now this book starts where the previous book, <i>Ash Princess</i> left us. <br/><br/>However, I feel like the characters didn't really do anything in this book but when s</span>
  <span id="freeText17516372049906015147" style="display:none">It was good.. but god dammit - I hate love triangles. <br /><br />Okay, I keep changing my mind on this freaking book rating. I can't decide to put a 3 or 4 star... so it'll be a freaking 3.5. Like I mentioned above, <i>Lady Smoke</i> was a good book. I have the audio version, which definitely makes it a bit easier for myself when working such long drastic hours. Now this book starts where the previous book, <i>Ash Princess</i> left us. <br /><br />However, I feel like the characters didn't really do anything in this book but when something actually exciting did.. it just felt a bit anti-climactic for me? Again, this could just be me. Then there's that freaking love triangle and I just couldn't stop eye rolling. I hate those things and I wish books would stop freaking using them. They are just frustrating to read about and at one point I just stop caring about the characters.<br /><br />The one thing that saved this book was the ending. I loved it and now I have so many questions forming in my mind. I have no idea when the third book is going to be an actual thing.. but I really need it now! I need answers ASAP!</span>

<div id="review_2499251857" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2499251857" />
    <a title="Tekla ✨" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3587456-tekla"><img alt="Tekla ✨" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594926257p2/3587456.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2499251857?book_show_action=true">Aug 25, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tekla ✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tekla ✨" href="/user/show/3587456-tekla">Tekla ✨</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3587456-tekla?shelf=books-2019">books-2019</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2499251857" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13772875041585781791">Spoilers for Lady Smoke hereunder.<br/><br/><br/><br/><i>“I hope you come to see that a woman can wield power beyond what’s between her legs—for your daughter’s sake if nothing else.”</i><br/><br/><i>“There’s a reason you can’t find the word virginity in Astrean. The concept doesn’t exist.”</i><br/><br/>~ ~ ~<br/><br/>These books are addictive. Even flawed, I just couldn’t stop reading.<br/><br/><b>This was so much better than I expected.</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1550067278ra/27057318.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/>Theo became such a complex and rich character. I loved how grey she was in so many areas. Loved her journey into finding who she was an</span>
  <span id="freeText13772875041585781791" style="display:none">Spoilers for Lady Smoke hereunder.<br><br><br><br><i>“I hope you come to see that a woman can wield power beyond what’s between her legs—for your daughter’s sake if nothing else.”</i><br><br><i>“There’s a reason you can’t find the word virginity in Astrean. The concept doesn’t exist.”</i><br><br>~ ~ ~<br><br>These books are addictive. Even flawed, I just couldn’t stop reading.<br><br><b>This was so much better than I expected.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1550067278ra/27057318.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>Theo became such a complex and rich character. I loved how grey she was in so many areas. Loved her journey into finding who she was and what kind of queen she would become. <br><br>As someone who’s been reading YA for a long time, I’m so pleased to notice certain changes in the gender. For example the female protagonists have their own agenda now in a way they never did before. We get a lot more representation, a feminist message, less toxic relationships... As someone who appreciates all these changes, I loved this book for all these things.<br><br><i>“I know him and he knows me and the darkest parts of our souls match.”</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1517041834ra/24943464.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>The relationship with Soren was so. good. He’s still too perfect for my taste but he was a lot better in this book. Loved their relationship development. They shared some really amazing quotes, and the level of intimacy, understanding and acceptance was just exactly what I’m into in a romance.<br><br>Heron and Erik. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1550067431ra/27057332.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>Hopefully they get more development in the last book. Their banter and filtration was delightful.<br><br>Hoa. I really, really loved her. And her scenes with Theo... They moved me.<br><br>Art. I loved how her relationship with Theo kept growing and become stronger as the book processed. FEMALE FRIENDSHIPS HELL YEAH~<br><br><br><b>But this was also worse than I expected.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1530856781ra/25930619.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>The story dragged too much on the “let’s find a husband with armies for Theo” plot, which was as bad as I had anticipated. And then rushed through the second half of the book, where admittedly the most interesting things happened.<br><br>Not. Enough. Cress. And the little we got was kind of a let down. Sure, her plot still got some of those trails typically chosen for male characters but then the author chose to portrait her as driven by her jealousy over a boy and I just- MEH.<br><br>I haaaaaate that she kidnapped Soren. She saw her father die by her friend, almost died herself, married the Kaiser, and who knows what else happened to her and she still cares about <i>a boy</i>. <br><br>Girl I thought you were smarter.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1445740319ra/16698295.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>The way the Kaiser died was just so cheap. He’s the BIG BAD and he dies like that? I understand now the villain is Cress and she and Theo are going to have a big fight in the last book. But still, that was pretty mediocre.<br><br> Also the guards saw Cress killing the Kaiser and they still followed her orders? So iffy.<br><br>The love triangle was awful. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1493047797ra/22578454.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>She chose Soren but still toyed with Blaise because she didn’t want to let him go. Kind of in a “I need everyone to love me” way that didn’t sit well with me.<br><br>The way she thought of Blaise was as family. Sure, she loved him. But not romantically. So whenever she mislead him in some way, or just let him take his own conclusions, it just irked me. <br><br>I understand the book is all about being morally grey, or how no one is all good or all bad. But Jesus h Christ, this was annoying.<br><br><b>Next book</b><br><br>I’m so interested in what will happen in the mine, but at the same time I liked the fact that Theo had no real powers and yet she was helping her people and freeing them. There’s something very compelling in reading about an ordinary person managing extraordinary things. But if she comes out of the mines now with like super powers, it’s going to cheapen it all a bit.<br><br>But again, I want to know more about the mines, the gems, the powers... I hope we get more explanations in the next book.<br><br>Overall, a really fun read!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="13772875041585781791" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer5928822770053117807">SPOILERS AHEAD<br/><br/><br/>3.5 stars rounded down. The first book was mesmerising, this was mediocre.<br/><br/>Here we meet Theo from where we left her, however she just doesn’t seem to progress as a character throughout this book at all. She still acts like a petulant teenager even though she is adamant she is a queen. I understand why Dragonsbane treats her they way she does.<br/><br/>I’m also becoming bored of the love triangle. I get it. We all get it. We all know how that’s gonna end.<br/><br/>The ending of the book was the most exc</span>
  <span id="freeText5928822770053117807" style="display:none">SPOILERS AHEAD<br /><br /><br />3.5 stars rounded down. The first book was mesmerising, this was mediocre.<br /><br />Here we meet Theo from where we left her, however she just doesn’t seem to progress as a character throughout this book at all. She still acts like a petulant teenager even though she is adamant she is a queen. I understand why Dragonsbane treats her they way she does.<br /><br />I’m also becoming bored of the love triangle. I get it. We all get it. We all know how that’s gonna end.<br /><br />The ending of the book was the most exciting part. The ending of her time travelling I didn’t see coming.<br /><br />The beginning of her return, I also did not see the choices that were made coming. Props to the author for that.<br /><br />Otherall, it was enjoyable but I’ll only be reading the final book to round off the trilogy, than out of sheer excitement for what’s coming next.</span>

  <span id="freeText11148954519829666405" style="display:none">I really liked Ash Princess but Lady Smoke was much better! This one was intense and you are more invested in the characters and plot so the 500+ pages just fly by. Readers will grow more attached to the characters in this one than they were in the first, but a couple things were predictable. However, the predictability did not take anything away from the story or the enjoyment of the story. Just a very good sequel and that ending…oh my! Cress got to go though. She a bit overdone now…<br /><br />My quick and simple overall: really satisfying sequel that leaves readers waiting for book three ASAP. <br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer770691935424738232"><b> 4 Stars!! </b><br/>🌟🌟🌟🌟<br/><br/><b>
  <i>“A queen without a crown, without a throne, without a coronation. What, exactly, do you imagine you're queen of?” </i>
</b><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1549995655ra/27053217.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Lady Smoke picks up right where Ash Princess left off. Theo is trying to get everything in order on her travels with Dragons-bane and her fleet. They are all looking for allies to take down the Kaiser and Cress. <br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1499278303ra/23212338.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>
  <u>Things I Liked:</u>
</b><br/>Theo shows a ton of growth in this book as her character falls in line with the title of Queen. Shes starting to come into herself and r</span>
  <span id="freeText770691935424738232" style="display:none"><b> 4 Stars!! </b><br>🌟🌟🌟🌟<br><br><b>
  <i>“A queen without a crown, without a throne, without a coronation. What, exactly, do you imagine you're queen of?” </i>
</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1549995655ra/27053217.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Lady Smoke picks up right where Ash Princess left off. Theo is trying to get everything in order on her travels with Dragons-bane and her fleet. They are all looking for allies to take down the Kaiser and Cress. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1499278303ra/23212338.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <u>Things I Liked:</u>
</b><br>Theo shows a ton of growth in this book as her character falls in line with the title of Queen. Shes starting to come into herself and really see what kind of leader she will make. She has lots of hard decisions to make and she is learning everything as she goes along. <br><br>My ship.... oh my ship .... ITS STILL KICKING!! Things may be a little rocky but Im telling you Im going down with this one!! <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1484061848ra/21678768.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>The Shadows </b>- They bring so much more to the book! I just love them- Heron, Blaise and Art all protect and handle Theo in their own individual ways. Art doesnt take any crap and is always mouthing off to her, but at the same time has Theo's back no matter what. Heron is quiet - yet he also will stand up to Theo when he is not on board with something. Blaise.... will do anything for Theo even if it means he has to pay with his life. He loves her and is so loyal- as her oldest friend- these two have an unbreakable bond. <br><br>The ending... I NEED BOOK 3 now!!!! <br><br><u>
  <b>What I didn't really like:</b>
</u><br><br>Some parts dragged a bit unlike the first book. There was also something major that happens towards the end - and the way it was handled had me scratching my head.. like is this really how this is about to go down?? I needed something bigger after everything Theo went through. I dont want to spoil anything but I personally needed this person to be put through HELL.. And maybe he was a little but not to my satisfaction. It just felt a bit lazy. <br><br>Lady Smoke was a really good read. I have seen some people like this one more than Ash Princess. But for me, I find that Lady Smoke suffered a little bit of middle book syndrome. I cant put my finger on what it was, but something was missing. Im not worried though- I think whatever it was will come back in full force once I read the final book. I still 100% recommend this series!</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2805528413" />
    <a title="Sophie &quot;Beware Of The Reader&quot;" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18451976-sophie-beware-of-the-reader"><img alt="Sophie &quot;Beware Of The Reader&quot;" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1424022406p2/18451976.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2805528413?book_show_action=true">May 01, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sophie &quot;Beware Of The Reader&quot;" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sophie &quot;Beware Of The Reader&quot;" href="/user/show/18451976-sophie-beware-of-the-reader">Sophie &quot;Beware Of The Reader&quot;</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2805528413" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15138324444738392268">Buddy read with Angy.<br/><br/>I read it in two days as I really was immersed into the story. It was slower in the beginning as I had to remember everything that had happened in the first book and who was who.<br/><br/>I like Theodosia better in this second book. She has matured and changed from the frightened little girl. Being far from the Kaiser is helping her of course. I like that she is experienced in navigating royal court and gives as good as she gets all with a saccharine smile. Yet she never loses sight o</span>
  <span id="freeText15138324444738392268" style="display:none">Buddy read with Angy.<br /><br />I read it in two days as I really was immersed into the story. It was slower in the beginning as I had to remember everything that had happened in the first book and who was who.<br /><br />I like Theodosia better in this second book. She has matured and changed from the frightened little girl. Being far from the Kaiser is helping her of course. I like that she is experienced in navigating royal court and gives as good as she gets all with a saccharine smile. Yet she never loses sight of the big picture and her goal to free her people. You could say she has an iron hand in a velvet glove. She will play the idiot and frivolous Queen to have others underestimate her. Even if she wants to bash some skull each time the king calls her “my dear” LOL<br />She is ready to sacrifice her happiness for her people yet she would never sacrifice her friends. Loyalty is another of her traits that I admire most.<br /><br />My only “dislike” is the pace. We spend a very long time in Sta’Crivero when Theodosia is meeting with suitors. I would not say nothing happened as it would not be true: you have assassination, the discovery of the camps, the strategizing, the progression of Blaise’s “illness” … but once they’ll be out (I won’t say much) everything will happen so fast, leaving me frustrated. And of course the cliffy because I hate cliffy LOL But in a series that’s unavoidable.<br /><br />I wonder how the next book will play out. I hope Theodosia will succeed in what she wants to do (shhhh not telling more). I also think she has much to grow into but I so love the woman she is becoming. So far from the frightened puppet child!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15138324444738392268" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2736261181" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2736261181" />
    <a title="Caylynn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66237296-caylynn"><img alt="Caylynn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594527171p2/66237296.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2736261181?book_show_action=true">Mar 04, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Caylynn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Caylynn" href="/user/show/66237296-caylynn">Caylynn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66237296-caylynn?shelf=ya-fantasy">ya-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66237296-caylynn?shelf=2019-release">2019-release</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2736261181" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6960884089662476831"><b>Reread review- I feel as though I should have waited another day to reread these two books because I CANNOT WAIT TWO MORE DAYS UNTIL <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/39216077.Ember_Queen__Ash_Princess_Trilogy___3_' title='Ember Queen (Ash Princess Trilogy, #3) by Laura Sebastian' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ember Queen</a>!!! I CAN'T DO IT, GUYS. I need this conclusion, guys.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1495814698ra/22858376.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>But yeah. This was definitely still a 5/5 star read, even though I'm dying for the conclusion. If-for some reason- you haven't picked up this trilogy yet, DO IT.</b><br/>----------------------------------------------<br/><i>
  <blockquote>Soren clenches his jaw and yanks the man's arms until he cries out. "Her name is Queen Theod</blockquote></i></span>
  <span id="freeText6960884089662476831" style="display:none"><b>Reread review- I feel as though I should have waited another day to reread these two books because I CANNOT WAIT TWO MORE DAYS UNTIL <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/39216077.Ember_Queen__Ash_Princess_Trilogy___3_" title="Ember Queen (Ash Princess Trilogy, #3) by Laura Sebastian" rel="nofollow noopener">Ember Queen</a>!!! I CAN'T DO IT, GUYS. I need this conclusion, guys.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1495814698ra/22858376.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But yeah. This was definitely still a 5/5 star read, even though I'm dying for the conclusion. If-for some reason- you haven't picked up this trilogy yet, DO IT.</b><br>----------------------------------------------<br><i>
  <blockquote>Soren clenches his jaw and yanks the man's arms until he cries out. "Her name is Queen Theodosia, and if you won't apologize for disrespecting her, I'll let her men have you and I'll describe your last moments to your wife so that she knows how pathetically you died."<br><br>Mattin grunts, eyes dropping away. "I apologize."<br><br>"I accept your apology," I say coldly. "I hope you come to see that a woman can wield power beyond what's between her legs- for your daughter's sake if nothing else."</blockquote>
</i><br>Well, hot damn. Lemme tell you something. There is definitely <i>NO</i> Second Book Syndrome in <i>this</i> trilogy, thank you very much.<br><br>And LOOK at that POWER COUPLE. Soren/Theo for LIFE.<br><br>But really, though. <i>Everyone</i> in this book fucking levels UP. It's like looking at a side-by-side of Dany, Cersei, Arya and Jon from Game of Thrones from season 1 and season 7. This group of rebels has<br><br>Not.<br>Come.<br>To.<br>PLAY.<br>GAMES.<br><br>This sequel takes place pretty much <i>right</i> after the events at the end of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32505753.Ash_Princess__Ash_Princess_Trilogy___1_" title="Ash Princess (Ash Princess Trilogy, #1) by Laura Sebastian" rel="nofollow noopener">Ash Princess</a>. Like, a few hours later. Now that Theo has escaped from the Kaiser with the help of her friends and Prinz Soren, she takes Soren "hostage" and utilizes the help of the pirate known as Dragonsbane to flee to a country on the other side of the world. Well, I <i>think</i> Sta'Crivero is the "other side of the world". Hypothetically.<br><br>Once Theo and her little band of rebels arrives to Sta'Crivero, she is quickly swept up in a bunch of "suitor" events, since Dragonsbane has convinced Theo that she needs to marry a strong country in order to have the power to take her kingdom back and free her people. Cue the drama, tension, and bitchy quotes <i>you'll</i> want to use in response to unwanted advances. <br><br>This was kind of a weird, slightly similar, convoluted version of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10507293.The_Selection__The_Selection___1_" title="The Selection (The Selection, #1) by Kiera Cass" rel="nofollow noopener">The Selection</a>? Except BETTER? I really don't know how to describe this story. Just that it is DAMN good. And the plot still moves along at a nice pace.<br><br>In the sequel, we get a shit ton of character development. We learn about the motivations behind more of the characters, like Soren, Dragonsbane, Artemisia, Heron, Erik and Blaise. Everyone gets closer, especially Theo, her crew, and Soren. Seriously, they have some cute sleepover scenes at the palace in Sta'Crivero that I absolutely loved. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/15945524.Laura_Sebastian" title="Laura Sebastian" rel="nofollow noopener">Laura Sebastian</a> does an incredible job of balancing out the severity of the situation Theo is in, and lighthearted scenes with her friends.<br><br>Theo makes mistakes, obviously, but she also <i>learns</i> from them. She doesn't give up, she changes to use the situation she's in and the people she is with to her advantage. She's also dealing with the consequences of spending ten years under the thumb of the Kaiser. She and Soren both spend a good chunk of this book wondering if the Kaiser has negatively affected both of them in a more permanent way than, say, PTSD.<br><i>
  <blockquote>I turn to Soren. "Do you still worry that you're the same as your father?"<br>"Not as much as I used to, but still often enough. Why?"<br>"Sometimes I worry I'm like him, too. He's left his mark on me, not just my body or my mind but my soul as well. Sometimes I worry he shaped me."</blockquote>
</i><br>I don't know. To me a huge theme of this book is facing the consequences of actions, ones that have already happened, and ones that are currently happening. It's something that I hardly ever see in YA novels, so this is <i>SO refreshing</i>. Theo accepts that things are the way they are now and that there's no going back, but that doesn't mean that she can't use what's happened to further her cause.<br><i>
  <blockquote>"I died the Queen of Peace, and peace died with me," she says after a moment. "But you are the Queen of Flame and Fury, Theodosia, and you will set their world on fire.</blockquote>
</i><br>Just give me the last book, already!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6960884089662476831" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_review_2736261181'><a id="like_count_review_2736261181" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/2736261181?resource_type=Review"><span class="likesCount">15 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it gr-button gr-button--small" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F40702154-lady-smoke">Like</a></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2585208560" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2585208560" />
    <a title="Kate (Feathered Turtle Press)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20798792-kate-feathered-turtle-press"><img alt="Kate (Feathered Turtle Press)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495666853p2/20798792.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2585208560?book_show_action=true">Dec 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kate (Feathered Turtle Press)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kate (Feathered Turtle Press)" href="/user/show/20798792-kate-feathered-turtle-press">Kate (Feathered Turtle Press)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2585208560" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5768897354484279095"><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>She takes another drink, a smaller one this time, before looking at me thoughtfully. “You’re lucky that you didn’t really know her.”<br/><br/>“Did you just say that I’m lucky my mother died?”<br/><br/>“I didn’t say that,” Dragonsbane says, rolling her eyes. “But it’s nice, in a way, to have her preserved so purely in your memory—a perfect mother and a perfect queen, brilliant and kind and valiant. She’s practically a goddess in your mind, isn’t she?"</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1548143886i/26953562.png' alt='00 high points final' width='176' height='55' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>– Actual progress toward Theo reclaiming her country n</span>
  <span id="freeText5768897354484279095" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>She takes another drink, a smaller one this time, before looking at me thoughtfully. “You’re lucky that you didn’t really know her.”<br><br>“Did you just say that I’m lucky my mother died?”<br><br>“I didn’t say that,” Dragonsbane says, rolling her eyes. “But it’s nice, in a way, to have her preserved so purely in your memory—a perfect mother and a perfect queen, brilliant and kind and valiant. She’s practically a goddess in your mind, isn’t she?"</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1548143886i/26953562.png" alt="00 high points final" width="176" height="55" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>– Actual progress toward Theo reclaiming her country near the end<br>– Varied settings<br>– The teeny, tiny subplot on how Theo remembers her mother<br>– Some characters receive adequate characterization<br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1548143886i/26953563.png" alt="00 low points final" width="156" height="50" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>– TELLING OVER SHOWING EVERY TWO SECONDS<br>– Author has no clue how to tell a story<br>– Plot lacks focus / loose storytelling<br>– Multiple inconsistencies<br>– Choice of first person POV + single POV detrimental to the story<br>– Over half the book is deadweight<br>– Literally deadweight, the first three chapters could be scrapped to no ill effect<br>– Every other girl (or woman) in the book is more interesting than Theo<br>– Theo is a weak, whiny, wishy-washy character<br>– The characters, collectively, share one brain cell<br>– Weak, hurried, sloppy prose<br><br><strong>If <em>Ash Princess</em> was <em>already</em> creatively bankrupt, then <em>Lady Smoke</em> is in the red.</strong> It's a book as empty of originality as the first, but somehow lacking more in substance, and completely devoid the overarching #edgy undertones and forbidden romance of the first.<br><br>Which, notedly, weren't the greatest, but at least they held the story together.<br><br><strong><em>Lady Smoke</em> is a bland, wasteful mess.</strong> Both plotting and prose reek of a lack of experience and practice. It reads as though the author word-vomited the entire thing from start to finish without stopping to think about a goddamn thing. It reads as if anyone who knows anything about writing or books or storytelling was beaten back from a stick. If an editor did anything to this, it's impossible to tell. The only way to fix <em>Lady Smoke</em> is to toss the whole thing out.<br><br>At nearly 130K words, <em>Lady Smoke</em> offers up a lot of useless garbage instead of plot. The prologue and first three chapters offer <em>nothing—</em>Theo reestablishes her circumstances in the most longwinded way possible. The first fifteen chapters offer very little and could be compressed into two or three instead, cutting out the overblown prose and nonsense, stripping it right down to the necessities. Even then, the pacing and shape of the plot are abysmal. <em>Ash Princess</em> was predictable, but at least the plotting was clean. <strong>There is very little meaningful plot here, and what little there is adds up to an ungainly whole.</strong><br><br>Sure, the characters <em>do</em> things, as in they occupy the pages, but they do very little to push the plot forward. Basically, Theo (and company) arrive in Sta’Crivero, Theo meets suitors, Theo whines the entire time, someone murders a couple suitors, Theo whines some more, Theo realizes the alliances she's made with the two weakest factions possible might be good enough to start, Theo (and company) fuck off into the night and head back to Astrea.<br><br><strong>There are no hard decisions. No agony of committing to a course of action. There are no regrets and no sacrifices.</strong> Theo does nothing. She sits around and bitches about everything. She does not direct the plot and she does nothing to invite inspiration or sympathy. She's barely a protagonist. She's not even engaging in the romantic subplots as she does in the first book.<br><br>The closest thing to a cohesive thread of plot is the teeny, tiny subplot where Dragonsbane tells Theo she only has a child's memory of her mother and Theo needs to come to terms with how her memory of her perfect mother is not the reality. It's very nearly meaningful.<br><br><em>Lady Smoke</em> closes on a scrambled note: once Theo returns to Astrea, everything is rushed, random and confusing. I suppose a certain thing is a "plot twist." But it reads more like the author knew the reader was falling asleep and decided to throw in random drama.<br><br><strong>Remember when we thought "Lady Smoke" would refer to Crescentia? Yeah, no. It's another reference to Theo, because everything is about Theo. Even though Theo doesn't do shit.</strong> Again, I can't help but return to how first person is a poor choice for point of view for this series. Either have your main character pushing the plot forward or switch to characters who are. Even with that aside, there are still so many more interesting characters than Theo! The series would be infinitely better if we switched around and followed scarred Crescentia's marriage to the Kaiser or explored Art's painful relationship with her mother or Dragonsbane's own conflicting emotions related to Astrea and her family. Even Blaise would benefit—yes, we know he's unstable, he loves Theo, he'd do anything to protect her, but he's so flat and one-dimensional in this sense. It's literally like he doesn't give a shit about anyone else in his life, alive or dead.<br><br>I could rouse sympathy for Theo in the first book, but in <em>Lady Smoke</em> she's just annoying. She doesn't <em>do</em> anything! And she's developed a new habit of whining about everything!<br><br>She can't sit in mild discomfort for a few goddamn hours: <em>
  <strong>An hour or two. I stifle a groan. I can’t imagine sitting out here more than a few minutes, even if the chairs brought out for the royal family and me are comfortably padded and somewhat shaded with palm fronds. Between the hot sun and my aching head and the dress pinching my ribs, I feel like I’m going to pass out.</strong>
</em><br><br>She's hungover, yes, but she's also in the most comfortable spot possible for the event. No matter what the circumstance, she <em>always</em> finds something to complain about. <em>Always</em>.<br><br>Theo (and the rest of the cast) have lost a few brain cells along the way as well. Literally every time Theo has a critical or strategizing thought—<em>literally </em>any time she comes close to a glimmer of an intelligent thought—she backtracks with an "omg, I'm using people, this means I'm like the Kaiser, bad Theo!"<br><br><strong>No, hon. That's just using your brain.</strong><br><br>Although we finally leave Astrea and Theo's claustrophobic room in the palace, what we explore of the setting is mediocre. Soren throws out one or two interesting facts about the other countries and their rulers, but it's a quick, slapdash effort to distinguish them from each other as they're dumped upon us. <strong>The names of other countries are clearly made up quickly and without thought, and hard to distinguish on the fly.</strong> Additionally, the country we actually spend time in—Sta’Crivero—is presented without nuance. No place will be perfect, but the things we learn about Sta’Crivero are only for Theo to complain about. It's as if the world is divided between the "good" conquered countries who have "nice" customs and the rest of the world, who all have bad customs and mean citizens.<br><br>It doesn't help that the author keeps throwing in stupid shit—stupid shit she clearly didn't think through or have a whole entire thought about beforehand or after. Example: every time Theo says she loves Soren's "driftwood" smell, I cringe. He smells like wood that's sat in water for weeks or months on end? Wood that's probably gone mildewy? And Theo likes that?<br><br>There's also this scene:<br><em>
  <strong>We’re in my room after lunch, finally having one of those lessons we discussed on the Smoke. I bore no illusions about my skills with a sword, but I expected Artemisia would at least go easy on me at first.</strong>
</em><br><br><em>
  <strong>No such luck. She hadn’t even wanted to use practice swords, though I’m glad I insisted—if our swords were sharp she would have killed me by now.</strong>
</em><br><br>Good lord, WHY? I want to scream and never stop screaming. Anyone with an ounce of competence or training WOULD NOT WANT TO USE REAL WEAPONS. Anyone with an ounce of competence or training WOULD NOT ENGAGE IN PRACTICE WITHOUT AT LEAST IMPROVISED PROTECTION. This whole section is cringe city! <strong>It shows, beyond a glimmer of a doubt, the author doesn't know SHIT and didn't bother to look LOOK UP SHIT either. </strong><br><br>The author's writing style is the worst of the lot: a run-on, rambling, near incoherent mess, taking a hammer to every rule for writing strong prose. The whole book reads like she banged out every thought crossing her head—and then a couple dozen more. Excessive filter words, weak verbs, passive voice, the utter ABUSE of adverbs. This author cannot write at all. Theo's telling over showing in every moment of every scene.<br><br><strong>Once again, the representation is highly questionable</strong>. The author clearly does not have the ability, forethought or grace to handle Theo's situation and history.<strong> (Of course, this series was never ABOUT exploring or discussing abuse. It's about excessive, voyeuristic angst.)</strong> There are characters of colour, but the handling of culture and such is horrifying. There are the Gorakians (who seem coded as South Asian) and the Vecturians (who might be coded as Indigenous Americans?) who are at least considered "good" people in the narrative's light. (Although the author doesn't seem to understand an "Emperor" denotes an "empire" and the Goraki have only two thousand people left and no Empire.) Sta’Crivero is very clearly coded as middle-eastern and hoooo boy. The rich Sta’Criverans are all wasteful fools and the poor Sta’Criverans are superstitious fools. Yikes. In terms of LGBT+ characters, Heron's storyline is reduced to his sexuality and another character is revealed awkwardly revealed as bi/pan for that burgeoning romance to take off. How lazy.<br><br><strong>On all fronts <em>Lady Smoke</em> is terrible. Why would you read it? Why did I read it? Why did someone let this be published? </strong></span>
  <a data-text-id="5768897354484279095" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2702695210" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18070543402920190626">I love this series all of it, writing style, setting, dialogues, characters, everything. The only thing I need explained is Theo/Blaise relationship, I don´t understand it and I think its written messily on purpose. </span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2707220124" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2707220124" />
    <a title="Rae" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3264820-rae"><img alt="Rae" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1516304743p2/3264820.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2707220124?book_show_action=true">Feb 12, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rae" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rae" href="/user/show/3264820-rae">Rae</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3264820-rae?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2707220124" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3082126834658727355">You can find this review and others on the blog here:<br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://vicariouslyvoraciously.com/reviews/book-review-lady-smoke/'>http://vicariouslyvoraciously.com/rev...</a><br/><br/><b>WARNING:This Review Contains Mild Spoilers for Ash Princess.</b><br/><br/>It's always the true test of a series if the second book can live up to the expectation that you were left with when you finished the first book. Will it have the same voice? Will the characters grow with the story? What will happen? Do you even care what happens next? And when you do finally get your hands on a copy of that book you've been wai</span>
  <span id="freeText3082126834658727355" style="display:none">You can find this review and others on the blog here:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://vicariouslyvoraciously.com/reviews/book-review-lady-smoke/">http://vicariouslyvoraciously.com/rev...</a><br /><br /><b>WARNING:This Review Contains Mild Spoilers for Ash Princess.</b><br /><br />It's always the true test of a series if the second book can live up to the expectation that you were left with when you finished the first book. Will it have the same voice? Will the characters grow with the story? What will happen? Do you even care what happens next? And when you do finally get your hands on a copy of that book you've been waiting on for months, or weeks, or even days (because let's be honest, no one likes to wait...) but regardless of how long you've waited you still want it to bring you back to that feeling you were left with that has had your mind constantly reminding you, hey remember that book?? Because those are the books that are the good ones, the ones that keep us wondering what happens next? So after I finished Ash Princess last year and my mind of course couldn't let me forget how I needed to find out what happens, I knew that Lady Smoke was going to be an easy decision to pick up and start reading it asap. And let me tell you, I was not let down! The wait was worth it. The voice is in fact, the same. The characters do grow with the story. And we do find out what happens next. I do care what happens in this story. At this point, I'm so involved with these characters and what they are doing that you might as well just sign me up for the third book now.. I'm hooked and I'm not afraid to admit it!<br /><br />Lady Smoke begins right where Ash Princess ends, on the ship owned by none other than pirate Dragonsbane who also happens to be Theo's aunt and Artemesia's mother. Now that Queen Theodosia has escaped with her life, her shadows, and prince Soren as her prisoner, the next step is to build an army to finally put an end to the Kaiser and all he stands for. But Dragonsbane has other plans in mind and they don't exactly line up with what Theo wants for her future. The question is, what is Theo willing to give up for her country? And how far will she go to save those who have been enslaved for too long?<br /><br />I liked that in this book we see more of the damage that the Kaiser has done. We see how vast his cruelty has spread and how he has his claws in everywhere spreading his hate. It makes him out to be even more despicable than you could possibly imagine him to be at first. This puts things on a grander scale for us and for our characters, because now its not just little ol Theo trying to escape a castle. Now we are dealing with entire countries who live in fear and poverty because they have been conquered by the Kalovaxians and it will take a lot more than one small crew of barely adults to help save them all. But that doesn't stop our MC. She is determined to do whatever it takes and still try and hold on to what she values while freeing her people and all those who have been crushed by the Kaiser she hates so much. I also can respect Theo because even through it all Soren is resigned to be her captive, knowing its true how his father has created so much death and destruction, and he is willing to shoulder it all for his love for Theo, but she won't let him wallow in self pity. She stands by him and trusts him even though she is told not to at every turn. There is something to be said for her tenacity and her will to see the good in people through all the bad that to me makes her the Queen they all say she isn't.<br /><br />The love triangle does continue in this book as it was in the first. With a little more angst and tension, but to be honest, if I was in Theo's position I wouldn't know who to choose either! I feel like one boy represents her past, and the other her future. But both of them hold an important role in Theo's life and she can't do without either of them. And then to add to the mix, the idea of an arranged marriage for a kingdom's army to help aid in her war with the Kaiser... She is just a mess of romance problems that I wouldn't with on my worst enemy. I feel bad for the poor girl, she definitely has her work cut out for her. But I will say that even through all the craziness, it is well done. You don't feel like she is making selfish decisions, but just dealing with the cards she's been dealt and trying to make the best of one awful situation after the next.<br /><br />There was a lot more in terms of action in this book too since now the Kaiser knows he's been had. And he plans to get his revenge, and the heads of Theo and Soren, dead or alive. With a few crazy twists that I wasn't expecting, it all comes to an epic battle and of course a cliffhanger to keep us crazy about this book until we can finally find out what happens in the last of the trilogy. I really enjoyed this one, I won't say it was better than the first but it was definitely just as good as. I find myself liking how I can get into these books and fly through them in a matter of a couple days and still feel like I read something worth while and exciting. I love a good romance with my books and these have kept my heart pitter pattering, butterflies and all. I want these characters to succeed. I do care what happens! And I can't wait for the next installment!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3082126834658727355" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
