<div id="review_2472045555" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2472045555" />
    <a title="Amanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/49013890-amanda"><img alt="Amanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1457622094p2/49013890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2472045555?book_show_action=true">May 07, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda" href="/user/show/49013890-amanda">Amanda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2472045555" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9191497525485244999">Review taken from <a href='http://literaryweaponry.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>Literary Weaponry</a><br/><br/>As you can see above, I rated this book 2.5/5 and that was being generous. So, all things considered, this is going to be more of a rant than anything else. <b>SPOILERS WILL FOLLOW.<br/><br/>~*~INCOMING SPOILERS~*~</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1557401842i/27477499._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Did I warn you enough about <b>spoilers</b>? Did you get the point? Good. Moving on.<br/><br/>I had preordered this book and received it on release day back in February. When I read Ash Princess, the first book in this trilogy, I had genuinely enjoyed it. There was an engaging plo</span>
  <span id="freeText9191497525485244999" style="display:none">Review taken from <a href="http://literaryweaponry.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Literary Weaponry</a><br><br>As you can see above, I rated this book 2.5/5 and that was being generous. So, all things considered, this is going to be more of a rant than anything else. <b>SPOILERS WILL FOLLOW.<br><br>~*~INCOMING SPOILERS~*~</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1557401842i/27477499._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Did I warn you enough about <b>spoilers</b>? Did you get the point? Good. Moving on.<br><br>I had preordered this book and received it on release day back in February. When I read Ash Princess, the first book in this trilogy, I had genuinely enjoyed it. There was an engaging plot that had a lot of room to be built upon and several characters with room and opportunity for amazing growth. I cracked open Lady Smoke just a few days ago very much looking forward to see that building and growth.<br><br>What I got was more of a trash fire and I am pretty pissed.<br><br>Just glancing back at the notes I took while reading this book, the very first one is from about 14% into the book and states,<br><br><i>“None of these characters have the combined sense to fill a teaspoon. How are they all so dim witted.”</i><br><br>Folks, it didn’t get much better from there.<br><br>Theodosia has her freedom from the Kaiser and intends to start a war to take back her kingdom with the help of her long lost pirate aunt and the aid of a rich, prosperous kingdom in exchange for her hand in marriage. Sounds like this plot could be exciting and entertaining, right?<br><br>WRONG!<br><br>Instead you are treated to page after page after page of whining, selfishness, short sightedness, and such an utter lack of sense that it is dumbfounding.<br><br>Theo determinedly says on multiple occasions that she will do anything to help her people, how much they mean to her, and how much she wishes to free her kingdom from the Kaiser’s rule. Of course, there are some stipulations to that. She turns up her nose and doesn’t want to see the conditions they have been forced to live in as refugees in whatever the heck kingdom it is that she is husband shopping in. I don’t care enough to look it up, the name is unimportant as is Theodosia.<br><br>That should be a first clue, right? If your supposed queen doesn’t want to see her people living in poor conditions, merely wants to visit them and make internal comments on the smell before returning back to the cushy palace, maybe she isn’t the best queen for the job, hm? Oh, and heaven forbid one of her entourage tries to visit the people, understand their plights and troubles, and be seen as a beacon of hope because Theo is sure going to complain about that, too. So inconvenient, she could have been back to the non smelly palace by now. Oh no!<br><br>There are no reasonable quotes to pull from this book so all quotes are going to come from my personal notes I took while reading…<br><br><i>“Hey, someone is trying to kill me. I should sneak around alone in the middle of the night and get into elevators with strange men three times my size! I’m such a brilliant queen.” -Theo the dimwit</i><br><br>You think I’m kidding but I’m not kidding. There was an attack on her life, in front of a room absolutely full of people and guards, and what does her dumb butt do? Go meandering around a strange palace in the middle of the night, getting into an elevator alone with a stranger, just to go get her flirt on with someone in a dungeon. Give. Me. A. Break. Any woman who has been alive more than five minutes knows better than to get into an elevator alone with a man ESPECIALLY if that man is three times your size, it is the middle of the night, and there is someone trying to kill you. How utterly stupid can you be?<br><br><i>I hate Theodosia so much. Calls herself queen but she only serves herself. A good queen does what is right, not only what serves her personal interests.</i><br><br>This happens over and over and over again throughout this book. She only thinks of herself. Only serves her own interests. Above I pointed out her being a spoiled little brat about the refugees living in squaller but I have more examples to share with you! One of her court or entourage or whatever she calls it is mine sick. If you’ve read Ash Princess you know what that is but for those that don’t remember, it means that you have extraordinary powers that you can’t control and can kill everyone around you and yourself. The person with this affliction intelligently goes, “Hey, maybe I shouldn’t be around people.” What does Theo do? Make him stay with her because of sentimentality. They were friends as a children, he helped save her from the Kaiser, so of course she can’t use common sense. That would simply be beyond the scope of her limited intelligence.<br><br>My 2.5 stars is genuinely probably more than this book deserves but I did give it a few points for the ending. In a nutshell there is a big battle and Theo isn’t a complete idiot. It was so refreshing! Thinking back, the battle wasn’t even that interesting or well written but it was so nice to not listen to whining and poor decision making for a couple of chapters that it was like reading gold.<br><br>There is so much else I could put in this review like the miserably written love triangle, killing the only character with half a teaspoon of sense, pretending that Theo is a strong character and then allowing her to get walked all over, and the plot that held on with only the most tenuous of grasp but I think that you all get my point.<br><br><i>Theo is stupid, selfish, self centered, and childish. Her court are short sighted and shallow minded fools. My dog has more sense than these simple minded plebeians.</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1557401842ra/27477500.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a href="http://literaryweaponry.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/literaryweapnry" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/literary_weaponry/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.amazon.com/hz/wishlist/ls/15UMSNEIJ14KF?ref_=wl_share" rel="nofollow noopener">Wish List</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="9191497525485244999" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I have been in a massive reading slump, which negatively affected my enjoyment of this book.   <span id="freeText10687237170643333776" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2110963219?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener"> Ash Princess </a>★★★★<br /><br /><b>3.5 STARS</b><br /><br />This was not the rating I was expecting to give this book. After completely adoring the first book, this book was a bit of a disappointment. To be fair, I can’t blame it entirely on the book. I have been in a massive reading slump, which negatively affected my enjoyment of this book. I also got extremely busy after starting this book, so I didn’t have time to finish.<br /><br />When I first read Ash Princess, I could not let go of it at all. I was completely engrossed, but I did not feel the same with this book. I still enjoyed it, and most of my thoughts stayed the same as in my review of Ash Princess, but I did not feel as encapsulated by the world and characters as the first book.<br /><br />As I said in my first review, this book does contain a lot of tropes, but they didn’t annoy me. One of those tropes was a love triangle, which I did not mind. Love triangles are the one trope that everyone except me seems to hate. In fact, sometimes, I even enjoy them. However, in this book, I could not stand it at all, which is unusual for me. It annoyed me so much and took away from the story. I feel like now I slightly understand why everyone hates them so much.<br /><br />But overall, it was a good sequel, and I know I am to blame for not enjoying it as much. I do own the final book, and I will be reading it very soon!</span>

<div id="review_3146337663" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3146337663" />
    <a title="Dilushani Jayalath" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42055091-dilushani-jayalath"><img alt="Dilushani Jayalath" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1468042052p2/42055091.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3146337663?book_show_action=true">Feb 18, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dilushani Jayalath" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dilushani Jayalath" href="/user/show/42055091-dilushani-jayalath">Dilushani Jayalath</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781509855186" href="/book/show/42392037-lady-smoke">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3146337663" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer265434240954709234">To say I am highly disappointed in this is an understatement. I cannot even say how much I disliked this book compared to the previous. I was in cloud 9 thinking that we finally got a headstrong female character where she does not let the factors such as romance and clandestine affairs affect her decisions. Clearly I thought too quick. It is as if Theo had taken 100 steps backwards in this book. I was dispirited while reading this. Everything I had in my head? Did a complete 180. I do not think </span>
  <span id="freeText265434240954709234" style="display:none">To say I am highly disappointed in this is an understatement. I cannot even say how much I disliked this book compared to the previous. I was in cloud 9 thinking that we finally got a headstrong female character where she does not let the factors such as romance and clandestine affairs affect her decisions. Clearly I thought too quick. It is as if Theo had taken 100 steps backwards in this book. I was dispirited while reading this. Everything I had in my head? Did a complete 180. I do not think anything in the final book could revive this back for me. <br /><br />The book catches just at the end of the last book and like I’ve been ranting on and on, this was just a mindless cluster-fuck. The story felt repetitive, the cliches were overused and the love triangle honestly just gave me a migraine. Did we have to bring such a triangle in here? She was doing so well on her own. Next is the utter childishness of our heroine. She kept mentioning to so many that she was the queen but j would have she rather acted it out and yes her options were limited but I think we heard more descriptions of her gowns/dresses than an actual handling of the dangers. It is as if the others had done by the time she arrived. <br /><br />At the end of Ash Princess I would have most definitely answered that I want the rest of the trilogy in one sitting if possible but by the end of Lady Smoke I am undoubtedly sure I would give it more time than diving head first to the third. A pity, in my opinion that is, this would have grown up for one of my all time favorite YA novels but I think it was never meant to achieve such heights.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2732375251" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2732375251" />
    <a title="Joshee Kun (조수아)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8832758-joshee-kun"><img alt="Joshee Kun (조수아)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574846759p2/8832758.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2732375251?book_show_action=true">Mar 14, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joshee Kun (조수아)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joshee Kun (조수아)" href="/user/show/8832758-joshee-kun">Joshee Kun (조수아)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781984851918" href="/book/show/44022083-lady-smoke">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8832758-joshee-kun?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8832758-joshee-kun?shelf=physically-owned">physically-owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8832758-joshee-kun?shelf=penguin-random-house">penguin-random-house</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2732375251" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12462792943390221874"><b>Thank you, Penguin Random House, for giving me a finished copy of this book in exchange for an honest review</b>.<br/><br/><i>My mother was the Queen of Peace. But I am not that sort of Queen</i>.<br/><br/>This sequel to <i>Ash Princess</i> was worth the wait. I've always loved political fantasies since they typically have enough intrigue to keep the pages flipping. With that in mind, <i>Lady Smoke</i> gave me the reading experience that I expected. Even though I didn't completely recall everything that happened in the first book, I didn't</span>
  <span id="freeText12462792943390221874" style="display:none"><b>Thank you, Penguin Random House, for giving me a finished copy of this book in exchange for an honest review</b>.<br /><br /><i>My mother was the Queen of Peace. But I am not that sort of Queen</i>.<br /><br />This sequel to <i>Ash Princess</i> was worth the wait. I've always loved political fantasies since they typically have enough intrigue to keep the pages flipping. With that in mind, <i>Lady Smoke</i> gave me the reading experience that I expected. Even though I didn't completely recall everything that happened in the first book, I didn't have a hard time getting back into Theo's dysfunctional world.<br /><br />The plot was probably one of the reasons for the latter phenomenon since it was somewhat reminiscent of <i>The Selection</i>, one of my favorite YA series. After Theo escaped from the clutches of the evil Kaiser and took refuge in Sta' Crivera, she desperately needed an army to back her up. Unfortunately, the only way to reach that goal was to marry a foreign royal, who would then claim a part of her beloved kingdom. Theo was unwilling to sacrifice her agency to any of her not-so-benevolent suitors, but she had no choice but to entertain their proposals. After all, the fate of Astrea was at stake. When Theo finally selects her future husband, something terrible happens, and she fears that it's the Kaiser's fault.<br /><br />Although the romantic/political drama was very familiar, I was too engaged to feel bored or jaded. Theo and her friends were always on edge, especially around the king of Sta' Crivera. Their alliance was shaky, so he could sell them out to the Kaiser if he thought that helping them was becoming inconvenient. Moreover, there was a malevolent force in the palace. If Theo didn't manage to find it, she would have to give up on procuring a powerful husband. I loved the irony of her situation. She had outsmarted the Kaiser only to face a similarly cunning enemy.<br /><br />Theo matured a lot in this book. By visiting one of the camps of her fellow refugees, she realized that there were people who had bigger problems than her. She also discovered the fatal flaw of her supposedly perfect mother. I liked that instead of feeling discouraged, she heeded the call of leadership; she strove to be strong and wise enough to give hope to those who had resigned themselves to poverty and suffering. In light her tenacity, it was no wonder that she had the affections of Blaise and Prince Soren. <br /><br />Compared to Theo, the two male leads were not that inspiring. Blaise had a suicidal streak or Messianic complex, while Soren had overrated daddy issues (and he was often a "lad in distress"). Also, the love triangle that they had with Theo bordered on emotional cheating. Still, I appreciated how they never failed to lift Theo's spirit through sincere words of affirmation. Without them, she would've succumbed to her bouts of self-doubt and pessimism.<br /><br />Dragonsbane, Theo's aunt, was the most complex character. I had some assumptions about her from the very beginning, and most of them turned out to be wrong. For a pirate, she sometimes had a striking sense of honor. Well, it was probably because her daughter (Artemisia) was Theo's close friend. Haha. Anyway, I'll try not to be judgmental toward fictional characters.<br /><br />With all that said, <i>Lady Smoke</i> was an utterly engaging combination of fantasy and politics. The fast pace made the book seem like it had less than 492 pages. I guess it would have been perfect without the overrated love triangle.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12462792943390221874" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('XF1C1uKrDjzCOay0k+j3oR0bTkV/YVVK2ZNsrYUhyEP09kjAtzuv+hlQkjv8xO9r7PDK/yCwRgtIawzHeFel+A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('kV6P0/J4qaHPi7DaO8vwT6sOHVewaCdlB5pet+H8gjA59YXFp+gIZxTijlVU5+iFWuWZ7e+5NCSWYj7dHIrviw==')})
  }
